     C G
People gather to re-establish their commitments for a better world and support each other in their grief. Candlelight vigils become powerful
    spaces for people to grieve those lost and
      make deep and enduring connections.
  M A  O
    ()
Labour-unions grown aer the destruction of the guilds by the State.—Their struggles.—Mutual aid in strikes.—Co-operation.—Free associations for various purposes.—Self-sacrice.—Countless societies for combined action under all possible aspects.—Mutual aid in slum-life.—Personal aid.
Whn w amin th vryday li o th rural populations o Europ, w nd that, notwithstanding all that has n don in modrn Stats or th dstruction o th villag community, th li o th pasants rmains honycomd with haits and customs o mutual aid and support; that important vstigs o th communal possssion o th soil ar still rtaind; and that, as soon as th lgal ostacls to rural association wr latly rmovd, a ntwork o r unions or all sorts o conomical purposs rapidly sprad among th pasants—th tndncy o this young movmnt ing to rconstitut som sort o union similar to th villag community o old. Such ing th conclusions arrivd at in th prcding chaptr, w hav now to considr, what institutions or mutual support can  ound at th prsnt tim among th industrial populations.
     For th last thr hundrd yars, th conditions or th growth o such
institutions hav n as unavoural in th towns as thy hav n in th villags. It is wll known, indd, that whn th mdival citis wr sudud in th sitnth cntury y growing military Stats, all institutions which kpt th artisans, th mastrs, and th mrchants togthr in th guilds and th citis wr violntly dstroyd. Th sl-govrnmnt and th sl-jurisdiction o oth th guild and th city wr aolishd; th oath o allgianc twn guild-rothrs cam an act o lony towards th Stat; th proprtis o th guilds wr conscatd in th sam way as th lands o th villag communitis; and th innr and tchnical organization o ach trad was takn in hand y th Stat. Laws, gradually growing in svrity, wr passd to prvnt artisans rom comining in any way. For a tim, som shadows o th old guilds wr tolratd: mrchants’ guilds wr allowd to ist undr th condition o rly granting susidis to th kings, and som artisan guilds wr kpt in istnc as organs o administration. Som o thm still drag on thir maninglss istnc. But what ormrly was th vital orc o mdival li and industry has long sinc disappard undr th crushing wight o th cntralizd Stat.
      In Grat Britain, which may  takn as th st illustration o th
industrial policy o th modrn Stats, w s th Parliamnt ginning th dstruction o th guilds as arly as th nth cntury; ut it was spcially in th nt cntury that dcisiv masurs wr takn. Hnry th Eighth not only ruind th organization o th guilds, ut also conscatd thir proprtis, with vn lss cus and mannrs, as Toulmin Smith wrot, than h had producd or conscating th stats o th monastris.1 Edward th Sith compltd his work,2 and alrady in th scond part o th sitnth cntury w nd th Parliamnt sttling all th disputs twn crasmn and mrchants, which ormrly wr sttld in ach city sparatly. With littl succss, it must  said; caus contsts and tchnical dicultis which wr arrangd or cnturis in succssion y agrmnt twn closly intrdpndnt guilds and dratd citis lay ntirly yond th powrs o th cntralizd Stat. Th continual intrrnc o its ocials paralyzd th trads; ringing most o thm to a complt dcay; and th last cntury conomists, whn thy ros against th Stat rgulation o industris, only vntilatd a widly lt discontnt. Th aolition o that intrrnc y th Frnch Rvolution was grtd as an act o liration, and th ampl o Franc was soon ollowd lswhr.
      With th rgulation o wags th Stat had no ttr succss. In th
mdival citis, whn th distinction twn mastrs and apprntics or journymn cam mor and mor apparnt in th nth cntury, unions o apprntics (Gesellenverbände), occasionally assuming an intrnational charactr, wr opposd to th unions o mastrs and mrchants. Now it was th Stat which undrtook to sttl thir gris, and undr th Elizathan Statut o  th Justics o Pac had to sttl th wags, so as to guarant a “convnint” livlihood to journymn and apprntics. Th Justics, howvr, provd hlplss to conciliat th conicting intrsts, and still lss to compl th mastrs to oy thir dcisions.      Thn coms in th allianc o th mothrs. “You could not imagin” (a

It is mntiond y all thos who hav livd among th poor. In a thousand small ways th mothrs support ach othr and stow thir car upon childrn that ar not thir own. “Whn th school childrn g rad, thy sldom or rathr nvr mt with a rusal”—a lady-rind, who has workd svral yars in Whitchapl in connction with a workrs’ clu, writs to m. But I may, prhaps, as wll transcri a w mor passags rom hr lttr:

     has littl childrn, and gos out or work, anothr mothr always

        I, in th working classs, thy would not hlp ach othr, thy

        D 
      C G
By collaborating in parking lots or abandoned
    works, people can tear up concrete and other
garbage to create local commons like playgrounds or community gardens. Former blight is transformed into a common treasury for the neighborhood.

## C

I w tak now th tachings which can  orrowd rom th analysis o modrn socity, in connction with th ody o vidnc rlativ to th importanc o mutual aid in th volution o th animal world and o mankind, w may sum up our inquiry as ollows.
      In th animal world w hav sn that th vast majority o spcis liv
in socitis, and that thy nd in association th st arms or th struggl or li: undrstood, o cours, in its wid Darwinian sns—not as a struggl or th shr mans o istnc, ut as a struggl against all natural conditions unavoural to th spcis. Th animal spcis, in which individual struggl has n rducd to its narrowst limits, and th practic o mutual aid has attaind th gratst dvlopmnt, ar invarialy th most numrous, th most prosprous, and th most opn to urthr progrss. Th mutual protction which is otaind in this cas, th possiility o attaining old ag and o accumulating princ, th highr intllctual dvlopmnt, and th urthr growth o social haits, scur th maintnanc o th spcis, its tnsion, and its urthr progrssiv volution. In th practic o mutual aid, which w can rtrac to th arlist ginnings o volution, w thus nd th positiv and undoutd origin o our thical concptions; and w can arm that in th thical progrss o man, mutual support not mutual struggl—has had th lading part.     W R
       J B
     By pooling courage and practical know-how,
people are able to liberate locked-up wealth and friends. As carceral facilities become increasingly
    militarized, jail breaks become more difcult.
Support for incarcerated people continues with a focus on posting bail, letter-writing, putting money on commissaries, advocating for individuals’ safety and release, and ensuring that as much as possible, people kidnapped by the state are not forgotten.

## A

I.—Swarms of Butterflies, Dragon-flies, etc. M.C. Piprs has pulishd in Natuurkunding Tijdschri voor Neederlandsch Indië, , Dl L. (analyzd in Naturwissenschaliche Rundschau, , vol. vi, ), intrsting rsarchs into th mass-ights o uttris which occur in Dutch East India, smingly undr th inunc o grat draughts occasiond y th wst monsoon. Such mass-ights usually tak plac in th rst months ar th ginning o th monsoon, and it is usually individuals o oth ss o Catopsilia (Callidryas) crocale, Cr., which join in it, ut occasionally th swarms consist o individuals longing to thr difrnt spcis o th gnus Euphoea. Copulation sms also to  th purpos o such ights. That ths ights ar not th rsult o concrtd action ut rathr a consqunc o imitation, or o a dsir o ollowing all othrs, is, o cours, quit possil.
       Bats saw, on th Amazon, th yllow and th orang Callidryas
“assmling in dnsly packd masss, somtims two or thr yards in circumrnc, thir wings all hld in an upright position, so that th ach lookd as though varigatd with ds o crocuss.” Thir migrating columns, crossing th rivr rom north to south, “wr unintrruptd, rom an arly hour in th morning till sunst” (Naturalist on the Amazon,).
       Dragon-is, in thir long migrations across th Pampas, com togthr
in countlss numrs, and thir immns swarms contain individuals longing to difrnt spcis (Hudson, Naturalist on the La Plata,  sq.).
       Th grasshopprs (Zoniopoda tarsata) ar also minntly grgarious
(Hudson, l.c., ).
II.—The Ants Pirr Hur’s Les fourmis indigènes (Gnèv, ), o which a chap dition was issud in  y Chruliz, in th Bibliothèque Genevoise, and o which translations ought to  circulatd in chap ditions in vry languag, is not only th st work on th sujct, ut also a modl o rally scintic
rsarch. Darwin was quit right in dscriing Pirr Hur as an vn gratr naturalist than his athr. This ook ought to  rad y vry young naturalist, not only or th acts it contains ut as a lsson in th mthods o rsarch. Th raring o ants in articial glass nsts, and th tst primnts mad y susqunt plorrs, including Luock, will all  ound in Hur’s admiral littl work. Radrs o th ooks o Forl and Luock ar, o cours, awar that oth th Swiss prossor and th British writr gan thir work in a critical mood, with th intntion o disproving Hur’s assrtions concrning th admiral mutual-aid instincts o th ants; ut that ar a carul invstigation thy could only conrm thm. Howvr, it is unortunatly charactristic o human natur gladly to liv any armation concrning mn ing al to chang at will th action o th orcs o Natur, ut to rus to admit wll-provd scintic acts tnding to rduc th distanc twn man and his animal rothrs.
      Mr. Suthrland (Origin and Growth of Moral Instinct) vidntly gan
his ook with th intntion o proving that all moral lings hav originatd rom parntal car and amilial lov, which oth appard only in warm-loodd animals; consquntly h tris to minimiz th importanc o sympathy and co-opration among ants. H quots Büchnr’s ook, Mind in Animals, and knows Luock’s primnts.       Mr. Suthrland dos not spciy which “ancdots” h mans, ut
it sms to m that h could nvr hav had th opportunity o prusing th works o Hur and Forl. Naturalists who know ths works nd no “ancdots” in thm.
      Th rcnt work o Prossor Gottrid Adlrz on th ants in Swdn
(Myrmecologiska Studier: Svenska Myror och des Lefnadsförhållanden, in Bihan till Svenska A kademiens Handlingar, Bd. Xi,. no. , ) may  mntiond in this plac.       Prossor G. Adlrz givs also vry intrsting primnts to prov
what Hur had alrady osrvd; namly, that ants rom two difrnt

      H also complts Forl’s and MacCook’s osrvations aout th

III.—Nesting Associations Auduon’s Journals (Audubon and his Journals, Nw York, ), spcially thos rlating to his li on th coasts o Larador and th St. Lawrnc rivr in th thirtis, contain cllnt dscriptions o th nsting associations o aquatic irds. Spaking o “Th Rock,” on o th Magdaln or Amhrst Islands, h wrot:—”At lvn I could distinguish its top plainly rom th dck, and thought it covrd with snow to th dpth o svral t; this apparanc istd on vry portion o th at, projcting shlvs. “But it was not snow: it was gannts, all calmly satd on thir ggs or nwly hatchd rood-thir hads all turnd windwards, almost touching ach othr, and in rgular lins. Th air aov, or a hundrd yards and or som distanc round th rock, “was lld with gannts on th wing, as i a havy all o snow was dirctly aov us.” Kittiwak gulls and oolish guillmots rd on th sam rock (Journals, vol. i. –).
       In sight o Anticosti Island, th sa “was litrally covrd with oolish
guillmots and with razorilld auks (Alca torva).” Furthr on, th air was lld with vlvt ducks. On th rocks o th Gul, th hrring gulls, th trns (grat, Arctic, and proaly Fostr’s), th Tringa pusilla, th sagulls, th auks, th Scotr ducks, th wild gs (Anser canadensis), th rd- rastd mrgansr, th cormorants, tc., wr all rding. Th sa-gulls wr trmly aundant thr; “thy ar or vr harassing vry othr ird, sucking thir ggs and dvouring thir young”; “thy tak hr th plac o agls and hawks.”
     On th Missouri, aov Saint Louis, Auduon saw, in , vulturs
and agls nsting in colonis. Thus h mntiond “long lins o lvatd shor, surmountd y stupndous rocks o limston, with many curious hols in thm, whr w saw vulturs and agls ntr towards dusk”—that is, Turky uzzards (Cathartes aura) and ald agls (Haliaëtus leucocephalus), E. Couës rmarks in a ootnot (vol. I, ).
     On o th st rding-grounds along th British shors ar th
Farn Islands, and on will nd in Charls Dion’s work, Among the Birds in Northern Shires, a livly dscription o ths grounds, whr scors o thousands o gulls, trns, idr-ducks, cormorants, ringd plovrs, oystrcatchrs, guillmots, and puns com togthr vry yar. “On approaching som o th islands th rst imprssion is that this gull (th lssr lack-ackd gull) monopolizs th whol o th ground, as it occurs in such vast aundanc. Th air sms ull o thm, th ground and ar rocks ar crowdd; and as our oat nally grats against th rough ach and w agrly jump ashor all coms noisy citmnt—a prct al o protsting cris that is prsistntly kpt up until w lav th plac” ().
IV.—Sociability of Animals That th sociaility o animals was gratr whn thy wr lss huntd y man, is conrmd y many acts showing that thos animals who now liv isolatd in countris inhaitd y man continu to liv in hrds in uninhaitd rgions. Thus on th watrlss platau dsrts o Northrn Thit Prjvalsky ound ars living in socitis. H mntions numrous “hrds o yaks, khulans, antlops, and vn ars.” Th lattr, h says, d upon th trmly numrous small rodnts, and ar so numrous that, “as th nativs assurd m, thy hav ound a hundrd or a hundrd and y o thm aslp in th sam cav” (Yearly Report o th Russian Gographical Socity or , ; Russian). Hars (Lepus Lehmani) liv in larg socitis in th Transcaspian trritory (N. Zarudnyi, Recherches zoologiques dans la contrée Transcaspienne, in Bull. Soc. Natur. Moscou, , ). Th small Caliornian os, who, according to E.S. Holdn, liv round th Lick osrvatory “on a mid dit o Manzanita rris and astronomrs’ chickns” (Nature, Novmr , ), sm also to  vry social.
     Som vry intrsting instancs o th lov o socity among animals
hav latly n givn y Mr. C.J. Cornish (Animals at Work and Play, London, ). All animals, h truly rmarks, hat solitud. H givs also an amusing instanc o th hait o th prairi dogs o kping sntris. It is so grat that thy always kp a sntinl on duty, vn at th London Zoological Gardn, and in th Paris Jardin d’Acclimatation ().
     Prossor Ksslr was quit right in pointing out that th young roods
o irds, kping togthr in autumn, contriut to th dvlopmnt o lings o sociaility. Mr. Cornish (Animals at Work and Play) has givn svral ampls o th plays o young mammals, such as, or instanc, lams playing at “ollow my ladr,” or at “I’m th king o th castl,” and thir lov o stplchass; also th awns playing a kind o “cross-touch,” th touch ing givn y th nos. Altogthr w hav, morovr, th cllnt work y Karl Gross, The Play of Animals.
V.—Checks to Over-Multiplication Hudson, in his Naturalist on the La Plata (chap. III), has a vry intrsting account o a suddn incras o a spcis o mic and o th consquncs o that suddn “wav o li.”
      “In th summr o –,” h writs, “w had plnty o sunshin,
with rqunt showrs, so that th hot months rought no darth o wild owrs, as in most yars.” Th sason was vry avoural or mic, and “ths prolic littl craturs wr soon so aundant that th dogs and th cats susistd almost clusivly on thm. Fos, wasls and opossums ard sumptuously; vn th insctivorous armadillo took to mic-hunting.” Th owls cam quit rapacious, “whil th sulphur tyrant-irds (Pitangus) and th Guira cuckoos pryd on nothing ut mic.” In th autumn, countlss numrs o storks and o short-ard owls mad thir apparanc, coming also to assist at th gnral ast. Nt cam a wintr o continud drought; th dry grass was atn, or turnd to dust; and th mic, dprivd o covr and ood, gan to di out. Th cats snakd ack to th houss; th short-ard owls—a wandring spcis—l; whil th littl urrowing owls cam so rducd as scarcly to  al to y, “and hung aout th houss all day long on th look-out or som stray morsl o ood. “Incrdil numrs o shp and cattl prishd th sam wintr, during a month o cold that ollowd th drought. As to th mic, Hudson maks th rmark that “scarcly a hard-prssd rmnant rmains ar th grat raction, to continu th spcis.”
       This illustration has an additional intrst in its showing how, on at
plains and plataus, th suddn incras o a spcis immdiatly attracts nmis rom othr parts o th plains, and how spcis unprotctd y thir social organization must ncssarily succum or thm.
       Anothr cllnt illustration in point is givn y th sam author rom
th Argntin Rpulic. Th coypu (Myiopotamus coypu) is thr a vry common rodnt—a rat in shap, ut as larg as an ottr. It is aquatic in its haits and vry social. “O an vning,” Hudson writs, “thy ar all out
swimming and playing in th watr, convrsing togthr in strang tuns, which sound lik th moans and cris o woundd and sufring mn. Th coypu, which has a n ur undr th long coars hair, was largly portd to Europ; ut som sity yars ago th Dictator Rosas issud a dcr prohiiting th hunting o this animal. Th rsult was that th animals incrasd and multiplid cdingly, and, aandoning thir aquatic haits, thy cam trrstrial and migratory, and swarmd vrywhr in sarch o ood. Suddnly a mystrious malady ll on thm, rom which thy quickly prishd, and cam almost tinct” ().
     Etrmination y man on th on sid, and contagious disass on
th othr sid, ar thus th main chcks which kp th spcis down—not comptition or th mans o istnc, which may not ist at all.
     Facts, proving that rgions njoying a ar mor congnial climat than
Siria ar qually undrpopulatd, could  producd in numrs. But in Bats’s wll-known work w nd th sam rmark concrning vn th shors o th Amazon rivr.”
     Thr is, in act,” Bats wrot, “a grat varity o mammals, irds and
rptils, ut thy ar widly scattrd and all cssivly shy o man. Th rgion is so tnsiv and uniorm in th orst-clothing o its surac, that it is only at long intrvals that animals ar sn in aundanc, whr som particular spot is ound which is mor attractiv than th othrs” (Naturalist on the Amazon, th d., ).
     This act is th mor striking as th Brazilian auna, which is poor in
mammals, is not poor at all in irds, and th Brazilian orsts aford ampl ood or irds, as may  sn rom a quotation, alrady givn on a prvious pag, aout irds’ socitis. And yt, th orsts o Brazil, lik thos o Asia and Arica, ar not ovrpopulatd, ut rathr undr-populatd. Th sam is tru concrning th pampas o South Amrica, aout which W.H. Hudson rmarks that it is rally astonishing that only on small ruminant should  ound on this immns grassy ara, so admiraly suitd to hr- ivorous quadrupds. Millions o shp, cattl and horss, introducd y man, graz now, as is known, upon a portion o ths prairis. Land-irds on th pampas ar also w in spcis and in numrs.
VI.—Adaptations to Avoid Competition Numrous ampls o such adaptations can  ound in th works o all ld-naturalists. On o thm, vry intrsting, may  givn in th hairy armadillo, o which W.H. Hudson says, that “it has struck a lin or itsl, and consquntly thrivs, whil its congnrs ar ast disapparing. Its ood is most varid. It prys on all kinds o inscts, discovring worms and
larva svral inchs nath th surac. It is ond o ggs and dglings; it ds on carrion as radily as a vultur; and, ailing animal ood, it su- sists on vgtal dit—clovr, and vn grains o maiz. Thror, whn othr animals ar starving, th hairy armadillo is always at and vigorous” (Naturalist on the La Plata, ).
      Th adaptivity o th lapwing maks it a spcis o which th rang o
tnsion is vry wid. In England, it “maks itsl at hom on aral land as radily as in wildr aras.” Ch. Dion says in his Birds of Northern Shires (), “Varity o ood is still mor th rul with th irds o pry.” Thus, or instanc, w larn rom th sam author (, ), “that th hn harrir o th British moors ds not only on small irds, ut also on mols and mic, and on rogs, lizards and inscts, whil most o th smallr alcons susist largly on inscts.”
      Th vry suggstiv chaptr which W.H. Hudson givs to th amily
o th South Amrican trcrprs, or woodhwrs, is anothr cllnt illustration o th ways in which larg portions o th animal population avoid comptition, whil at th sam tim thy succd in coming vry numrous in a givn rgion, without ing possssd o any o th wapons usually considrd as ssntial in th struggl or istnc. Th aov amily covrs an immns rang, rom South Mico to Patagonia, and no wr than  spcis, rral to aout  gnra, ar alrady known rom this amily, th most striking atur o which is th grat divrsity o haits o its mmrs. Not only th difrnt gnra and th difrnt spcis possss haits pculiarly thir own, ut vn th sam spcis is on ound to difr in its mannr o li in difrnt localitis. “Som spcis o Xenops and Magarornis, lik woodpckrs, clim vrtically on tr-trunks in sarch o insct pry, ut also, lik tits, plor th smallr twigs and oliag at th trmity o th ranchs; so that th whol tr, rom th root to its topmost oliag, is huntd ovr y thm. Th Sclerurus, although an inhaitant o th darkst orst, and providd with sharply curvd claws, nvr sks its ood on trs, ut clusivly on th ground, among th dcaying alln lavs; ut, strangly nough, whn alarmd, it is to th trunk o th narst tr, to which it clings in a vrtical position, and, rmaining silnt and motionlss, scaps osrvation y mans o its dark protctiv colour.” And so on. In thir nsting haits thy also vary immnsly. Thus, in on singl gnus, thr spcis uild an ovn-shapd clay-nst, a ourth uilds a nst o sticks in th trs, and a h urrows in th sid o a ank, lik a kingshr.
      Now, this trmly larg amily, o which Hudson says that “vry
portion o th South Amrican continnt is occupid y thm; or thr is
rally no climat, and no kind o soil or vgtation, which dos not possss its appropriat spcis, longs”—to us his own words—“to th most dnclss o irds.” Lik th ducks which wr mntiond y Syvrtsof (s in th tt), thy display no powrul ak or claws; “thy ar timid, unrsisting craturs, without strngth or wapons; thir movmnts ar lss quick and vigorous than thos o othr kinds, and thir ight is cdingly l.” But thy possss—oth Hudson and Asara osrv—“th social disposition in an minnt dgr,” although “th social hait is kpt down in thm y th conditions o a li which maks solitud ncssary.” Thy cannot mak thos larg rding associations which w s in th sa- irds, caus thy liv on th tr-inscts, and thy must carully plor sparatly vry tr—which thy do in a most usinss-lik way; ut thy continually call ach othr in th woods, “convrsing with on anothr ovr long distancs”; and thy associat in thos “wandring ands” which ar wll known rom Bats’s pictursqu dscription, whil Hudson was ld to liv “that vrywhr in South Amrica th Dndrocolaptida ar th rst in comining to act in concrt, and that th irds o othr amilis ollow thir march and associat with thm, knowing rom princ that a rich harvst may  rapd.” It hardly nd  addd that Hudson pays thm also a high complimnt concrning thir intllignc. Sociaility and intllignc always go hand in hand.
VII.—The Origin of the Family At th tim whn I wrot th chaptr insrtd in th tt, a crtain accord smd to hav n stalishd among anthropologists concrning th rlativly lat apparanc, in th institutions o mn, o th patriarchal amily, such as w know it among th Hrws, or in Imprial Rom. Howvr, works hav n pulishd sinc, in which th idas promulgatd y Bachon and MacLnnan, systmatizd spcially y Morgan, and urthr dvlopd and conrmd y Post, Maim Kovalvsky, and Luock, wr contstd—th most important o such works ing y th Danish prossor C.N. Starck (Primitive Family, ) and th Finnish prossor Edward Wstrmarck (The History of Human Marriage, ). Th sam has happnd with this qustion o primitiv marriag institutions as it happnd with th qustion o th primitiv land-ownrship institutions. Whn th idas o Maurr and Nass on th villag community, dvlopd y quit a school o gid plorrs, and thos o all modrn anthropologists upon th primitivly communistic constitution o th clan had narly won gnral accptanc—thy calld orth th apparanc o such works as thos o Fustl d Coulangs in Franc, th Oord Prossor Sohm

was rgardd as suprior to man, or was th “had” o th clan; this is a quit distinct mattr, and my prsonal opinion is that no such priod has vr istd; nor dos it prov that thr was a tim whn no trial

But whn all th acts latly rought to light ar considrd in thir mutual dpndncy, it is impossil not to rcogniz that i isolatd coupls, with thir childrn, hav possily istd vn in th primitiv clan, ths incipint amilis wr tolerated exceptions only, not th institution o th tim.
VIII.—Destruction of Private Property on the Grave In a rmarkal work, The Religious Systems of China, pulishd in – y J. M. d Groot at Lydn, w nd th conrmation o this ida. Thr was in China (as lswhr) a tim whn all prsonal longings o a dad prson wr dstroyd on his tom—his moiliary goods, his chattls, his slavs, and vn rinds and vassals, and o cours his widow. It rquird a strong raction against this custom on hal o th moralists to put an nd to it. With th gipsis in England th custom o dstroying all chattls on th grav has survivd up to th prsnt day. All th prsonal proprty o th gipsy qun who did a w yars ago was dstroyd on hr grav. Svral nwspaprs mntiond it at that tim.
IX.—The “Undivided Family” A numr o valual works on th South Slavonian Zadruga, or “compound amily,” compard to othr orms o amily organization, hav n pulishd sinc th aov was writtn; namly, y Ernst Milr (Jahrbuch der Internationaler Vereinung für vergleichende Rechtswissenscha und Volkswirthschaslehre, ), and I.E. Gszow’s Zadruga in Bulgaria, and Zadruga-Ownership and Work in Bulgaria (oth in Bulgarian). I must also mntion th wll-known study o Bogisic (De la forme dite ‘inokosna’ de la famille rurale chez les Serbes et les Croates, Paris, ), which has n omittd in th tt.
X.—The Origin of the Guilds Th origin o th guilds has n th sujct o many controvrsis. Thr is not th slightst dout that cra-guilds, or “collgs” o artisans, istd in ancint Rom. It appars, indd, rom a passag in Plutarch that Numa lgislatd aout thm. “H dividd th popl,” w ar told, “into trads . . . ordring thm to hav rothrhoods, stivals, and mtings, and indicating th worship thy had to accomplish or th gods, according to th dignity o ach trad.” It is almost crtain, howvr, that it was not th Roman king who invntd, or institutd, th trad-collgs—thy had alrady istd in ancint Grc; in all proaility, h simply sumittd
thm to royal lgislation, just as Philipp l Bl, n cnturis latr, su- mittd th trads o Franc, much to thir dtrimnt, to royal suprvision and lgislation. On o th succssors o Numa, Srvius Tullius, also is said to hav issud som lgislation concrning th collgs.3
     Consquntly, it was quit natural that historians should ask thmslvs whthr th guilds which took such a dvlopmnt in th twlh,
and vn th tnth and th lvnth cnturis, wr not rvivals o th old Roman “collgs”—th mor so as th lattr, as sn rom th aov quotation, quit corrspondd to th mdival guild.4 It is known, indd, that corporations o th Roman typ istd in Southrn Gaul down to th h cntury. Bsids, an inscription ound during som cavations in Paris shows that a corporation o Luttia nautae istd undr Tirius; and in th chart givn to th Paris “watr-mrchants” in , thir rights ar spokn o as isting ab antiquo (sam author, ). Thr would hav n, thror, nothing traordinary, had corporations n maintaind in arly mdival Franc ar th ararian invasions.
     Howvr, vn i as much must  grantd, thr is no rason to maintain that th Dutch corporations, th Norman guilds, th Russian artels, th
Gorgian amkari, and so on, ncssarily hav had also a Roman, or vn a Byzantin origin. O cours, th intrcours twn th Normans and th capital o th East-Roman Empir was vry activ, and th Slavonians (as has n provd y Russian historians, and spcially y Ramaud) took a livly part in that intrcours. So, th Normans and th Russians may hav importd th Roman organization o trad-corporations into thir rspctiv lands. But whn w s that th artel was th vry ssnc o th vryday li o all th Russians, as arly as th tnth cntury, and that this artel, although no sort o lgislation has vr rgulatd its li till modrn tims, has th vry sam aturs as th Roman collg and th Wstrn guild, w ar still mor inclind to considr th astrn guild as having an vn mor ancint origin than th Roman collg. Romans knw wll, indd, that thir sodalitia and collegia wr “what th Grks calld hetairiai” (Martin-Saint-Léon, ), and rom what w know o th history o th East, w may conclud, with littl proaility o ing mistakn, that th grat nations o th East, as wll as Egypt, also hav had th sam guild organization. Th ssntial aturs o this organization rmain th sam whrvr w may nd thm. It is a union o mn carrying on th sam pro- ssion or trad. This union, lik th primitiv clan, has its own gods and its own worship, always containing som mystris, spcic to ach sparat union; it considrs all its mmrs as brothers and sisters—possily (at its ginnings) with all th consquncs which such a rlationship implid
in th gns, or, at last, with crmonis that indicatd or symolizd th clan rlations twn rothr and sistr; and nally, all th oligations o mutual support which istd in th clan, ist in this union; namly, th clusion o th vry possiility o a murdr within th rothrhood, th clan rsponsiility or justic, and th oligation, in cas o a minor disput, o ringing th mattr or th judgs, or rathr th aritrs, o th guild rothrhood. Th guild—on may say—is thus modlld upon th clan.
       Consquntly, th sam rmarks which ar mad in th tt concrning
th origin o th villag community, apply, I am inclind to think, qually to th guild, th artel, and th cra- or nighour-rothrhood. Whn th onds which ormrly connctd mn in thir clans wr loosnd in consqunc o migrations, th apparanc o th patrnal amily, and a growing divrsity o occupations—a nw territorial bond was workd out y mankind in th shap o th villag community; and anothr ond—an occupation bond—was workd out in an imaginary rothrhood—the imaginary clan, which was rprsntd: twn two mn, or a w mn, y th “mitur-o-lood rothrhood” (th Slavonian pobratimstvo), and twn a gratr numr o mn o difrnt origin, i.. originatd rom difrnt clans, inhaiting th sam villag or town (or vn difrnt villags or towns)—th phratry, th hetairiai, th amkari, th artel, th guild.5
       As to th ida and th orm o such an organization, its lmnts wr
alrady indicatd rom th savag priod downwards. W know indd that in th clans o all savags thr ar sparat scrt organizations o warriors, o witchs, o young mn, tc.—cra mystris, in which knowl- dg concrning hunting or warar is transmittd; in a word, “clus,” as Miklukho-Maclay dscrid thm. Ths “mystris” wr, in all proaility, th prototyps o th utur guilds.6
       With rgard to th aov-mntiond work y E. Martin-Saint-Léon, lt
m add that it contains vry valual inormation concrning th organization o th trads in Paris—as it appars rom th Livre des métiers of Boileau—and a good summary o inormation rlativ to th Communs o difrnt parts o Franc, with all iliographical indications. It must, howvr,  rmmrd that Paris was a “Royal city” (lik Moscow, or Wstminstr), and that consquntly th r mdival-city institutions hav nvr attaind thr th dvlopmnt which thy hav attaind in r citis. Far rom rprsnting “th pictur o a typical corporation,” th corporations o Paris, “orn and dvlopd undr th dirct tutorship o royalty,” or this vry sam caus (which th author considrs a caus o supriority, whil it was a caus o inriority—h himsl ully shows in
difrnt parts o his work how th intrrnc o th imprial powr in Rom, and o th royal powr in Franc, dstroyd and paralyzd th li o th cra-guilds) could nvr attain th wondrul growth and inunc upon all th li o th city which thy did attain in North-Eastrn Franc, at Lyons, Montpllir, Nims, tc., or in th r citis o Italy, Flandrs, Grmany, and so on.
XI.—The Market and the Medieval City In a work on th mdival city (Markt und Stadt in ihrem rechtlichen Verhältnis, Lipzig, ), Ritschl has dvlopd th ida that th origin o th Grman mdival communs must  sought in th market. Th local markt, placd undr th protction o a ishop, a monastry or a princ, gathrd round it a population o tradsmn and artisans, ut no agricultural population. Th sctions into which th towns wr usually dividd, radiating rom th markt-plac and popld ach with artisans o spcial trads, ar a proo o that: thy ormd usually th Old Town, whil th Nw Town usd to  a rural villag longing to th princ or th king. Th two wr govrnd y difrnt laws.
     It is crtainly tru that th markt has playd an important part in th
arly dvlopmnt o all mdival citis, contriuting to incras th walth o th citizns, and giving thm idas o indpndnc; ut, as has n rmarkd y Carl Hgl—th wll-known author o a vry good gnral work on Grman mdival citis (Die Entstehung des deutschen Städtewesens, Lipzig, ), th town-law is not a markt-law, and Hgl’s conclusion is (in urthr support to th viws takn in this ook) that th mdival city has had a doul origin. Thr wr in it “two populations placd y th sid o ach othr: on rural, and th othr purly uran”; th rural population, which ormrly livd undr th organization o th Almende, or villag community, was incorporatd in th city.
     With rgard to th mrchant guilds, th work o Hrman van dn
Lindn (Les Gildes marchandes dans les Pays-Bas au Moyen Age, Gand, , in Recueil de travaux publiés par la Faculté de Philosophie et Lettres) dsrvs a spcial mntion. Th author ollows th gradual dvlopmnt o thir political orc and th authority which thy gradually acquird upon th industrial population, spcially on th draprs, and dscris th lagu concludd y th artisans to oppos thir growing powr. Th ida, which is dvlopd in this ook, concrning th apparanc o th mrchant guild at a latr priod which mostly corrspondd to a priod o dclin o th city lirtis, sms thus to nd conrmation in H. van dn Lindn’s rsarchs.
XII.—Mutual-Aid Arrangements in the Villages of Netherlands at the Present Day Th Rport o th Agricultural Commission o Nthrlands contains many illustrations rlativ to this sujct, and my rind, M. Cornlissn, was kind nough to pick out or m th corrsponding passags rom ths ulky volums (Uitkomsten van het Onderzoek naar den Toestand van den Landbouw in Nederland,  vols. ).
     Th hait o having on thrshing machin, which maks th round o
many arms, hiring it in turn, is vry widly sprad, as it is y this tim in narly vry othr country. But on nds hr and thr a commun which kps on thrshing machin or th community (vol. i. viii, ).
     Th armrs who hav not th ncssary numrs o horss or th
plough orrow th horss rom thir nighours. Th hait o kping on communal o, or on communal stallion, is vry common.
     Whn th villag has to rais th ground (in th low districts) in ordr
to uild a communal school, or or on o th pasants in ordr to uild a nw hous, a bede is usually convokd. Th sam is don or thos armrs who hav to mov. Th bede is altogthr a widly sprad custom, and no on, rich or poor, will ail to com with his hors and cart.
     Th rnting in common, y svral agricultural laourrs, o a madow,
or kping thir cows, is ound in svral parts o th land; it is also r- qunt that th armr, who has plough and horss, ploughs th land or his hird laourrs (vol. i. ii, , tc.).
     As to th armrs’ unions or uying sd, porting vgtals to
England and so on, thy com univrsal. Th sam is sn in Blgium. In , svn yars ar pasants’ guilds had n startd, rst in th Flmish part o th country, and our yars only ar thy wr introducd in th Walloon portion o Blgium, thr wr alrady  such guilds, with a mmrship o , (Annuaire de la Science Agronomique, vol. i. (), ,  and ).

By collaboratively creating conditions of anonymity the black bloc impedes the ability of state authorities
    and reactionaries to identify participants, as
well as signaling to others a willingness to strike back against that which oppresses us. Both the wider bloc and smaller afnity groups collectively
      work to keep one another safe, including
    stopping the police from kidnapping people.

## Allan Antliff

     The Arts and Cras movement has been really inuential on me. Walter
     Crane and William Morris’s work and criticism provide a lot of direction
     and inspiration for my approach to illustration and the projects that I am
     interested in realizing. —N.O. Bonzo
In , London’s Frdom Prss pulishd Kropotkin: Selections from His Writings, ditd y th anarchist art critic/historian, pot, and political thorist Hrrt Rad (–). Born into th Russian aristocracy and ducatd as a gographr, Ptr Kropotkin (–) was Europ’s lading proponnt o anarchist communism and an acclaimd scintist, who spnt considral tim in England.1 Rad’s introduction includs Emma Goldman’s (–) rminiscnc o hr last visit to Kropotkin’s hom in Dmitrov, Russia, on Fruary , , th day h did at ag ighty o pnumonia.2 H had rturnd to th country o his irth ollowing th ovrthrow o th Tsar (Empror o Russia) in Fruary , only to princ th sizur o Stat powr y Lnin’s Communist Party that Novmr (th so-calld Octor Rvolution) and th imposition o dictatorial policis antithtical to mutual aid.3 Having n harassd out o Moscow in th summr o  y Communist govrnmnt uraucrats, Kropotkin’s “involuntary il” to a small villag outsid th capital was plagud y privation, ut his crativity nvr wavrd.4 “During th two days I spnt in th Kropotkin houshold,” Goldman rlats,
     I larnd mor o his prsonal li than during all th yars that I
     had known him. Evn his closst rinds wr not awar that Ptr
     Kropotkin was an artist . . . o much talnt. Among his forts I discovrd a collction o drawings o grat mrit. . . . And now h lay
     on his couch, in th littl workroom, as i pacully aslp, his ac
     as kindly in dath as it had n in li.5
      Rad praisd Mutual Aid as “possily [Kropotkin’s] gratst ook”
and rprints passags rom it throughout his compndium.6 Most importantly or our purposs, h nds his Selections with a susction, “Art and Socity,” crptd rom The Conquest of Bread ().7 Hr w ncountr urthr vidnc o Kropotkin’s conviction that th arts ar important. H lamnts th divorc o art rom th communal li o th popl undr capitalism, writing “only whn citis, trritoris, nations, or groups o nations, will hav rnwd thir harmonious li, will art  al to draw its inspiration rom ideals held in common.”8 “Art,” h dclard, “must  ound up with industry y a thousand intrmdiat dgrs, lndd, so to say, as . . . th grat Socialist pot [William] Morris (–) . . . provd so on and so wll. Evrything that surrounds man, in th strt, in th intrior and trior o pulic monumnts, must  o pur artistic orm. But this can only happn in a socity in which all njoy comort and lisur. Thn only shall w s art associations, o which ach mmr will nd room or his capacity.”9 This visionary indtdnss to Morris, oundr o th intrnational Arts and Cras movmnt, mrits urthr ploration.10
      Kropotkin’s rst contact with Morris dats to .11 Ar a daring
scap rom Russian imprisonmnt in , Kropotkin spnt a harrid priod in il, mostly in Switzrland and Franc. Anarchist-rlatd activitis ld to pulsion rom Switzrland in , ollowd y a ri sojourn in England or rlocation to Franc. In  th Frnch govrnmnt sntncd him to v yars’ imprisonmnt or his politics and, upon gaining arly rlas in January , it was clar h could no longr rmain in that country, so h accptd th invitation o a group o London-asd anarchists to hlp ound a nwspapr to promot anarchist communism (Kropotkin would coound Freedom in ).12 Anarchism was thn gaining ground in th Unitd Kingdom, and th involvmnt o a rnownd gur alrady amous or his scintic work as wll as a myriad o anarchistrlatd ooks, pamphlts, articls, and journalistic contriutions was caus or clration. Within a w days o his arrival in arly March, Kropotkin was invitd to spak at an vnt organizd y th Socialist Lagu (– ) honouring th Paris Commun (), and this is whr h mt Morris, who was th Lagu’s driving orc and ditor o its journal, Commonweal.13
      Morris was an antiparliamntarian “communist” who, Ruth Kinna
summarizs, shard Kropotkin’s political vision o dcntralizd dralism ut dclind to join th movmnt on th grounds that it was taintd y “individualist” tndncis (advocating “trrorism” and “violnt rvolution” was also, tactically, prolmatic).14 Nvrthlss, anitis on trump difrncs. Ar thir rst mting, Morris wrot to a rind
rlating “Kropotkin nw com [sic] rom prison and I mad his acquaintanc . . . I lik him vry much.”15 Thrar Kropotkin was a rqunt visitor to Morris’s hom, Klmscott Hous, whr h mid with artists, printrs, mroidrrs, ook illustrators, writrs, pots, playwrights, and radicals.16 H also rindd Morris’s daughtr, May (–), who was thn in charg o th mroidry division o his artisan-asd multiactd usinss, Morris and Co. (–).17 Kropotkin was not th only anarchist Morris maintaind cordial rlations with. H hostd anarchist communism’s othr lading thorist, Elisé Rclus (–), at Klmscott Hous18 and collaoratd with Victor Dav (–), a Blgian who had d prscution to London, to co-author a Socialist Lagu pamphlt, A Short Account of the Paris Commune ().19 Jan Grav (–), ditor o th anarchist communist journals La Révolte (–) and its succssor, Les Temps Nouveaux (–), was on amiliar nough trms to ptition Morris or illustrations in  and solicit a rontispic dsign or a Les Temps Nouveaux portolio o artists’ lithographs in , not long or Morris did.20 And, in , Morris assistd Louis Michl (–), who had ought in th Paris Commun, to launch an anarchist-inspird school or childrn in London.21 In a rindly lttr to th anarchist communist typsttr Wol Wss (–) agring to support Kropotkin’s nwspapr, Freedom, Morris gntly suggstd most anarchists wr “socialists, only somwhat wrong-hadd, i I may say so, as to tactics.”22 This is th spirit in which h orgd anitis with th movmnt and, in , ackd an unsuccssul proposal that anarchist organizations participat in th Scond Intrnational.23
      Morris’s commitmnt to artisan-asd practics ncompassing
waving tapstris and rugs, dcorativ tils, urnitur manuactur, int- rior dcoration, jwlry-making, wallpapr and staind-glass production, woodlock ngraving, ttils, illustration, and ook pulishing, was drivn y his conviction that artisanship was th mans through which workrs in th dcntralizd communist utur would ostr a socity in which work was plasural and artistry prmatd vryday li.24 Similarly, as Royn Roslak osrvs, anarchist communists also advocatd “a utur socity structurd around small, sl-govrning communs whos conomis would  asd on an allianc o intnsiv agricultur, light industry, and skilld crasmanship.”25 In act, Rclus and Kropotkin “took an normous intrst in artisanal cultur” and liknd craspopl ngagd in “intllignt and carul laour” to “artists,” in contrast to actory workrs rducd to “auiliaris to th machin.”26 Artisanship, thy livd, could lirat work, and this accords with th passags slctd y Rad rom
The Conquest of Bread. Th oundational ond uniting Morris with th anarchist communists was thir shard admiration or th mdival ra’s guild-asd conomis and cooprativ artisanship as showcasd in Mutual Aid.27 Whatvr its aults, this ofrd a modl or th communist utur worth mulating.28
     W should not  surprisd, thn, to larn that anarchists took notic
o Morris’s last grat ndavor, th Klmscott Prss (–). Morris’s undrtaking was inspird, in part, y his sustantial collction o mdival illuminatd manuscripts and nth-cntury printd ooks.29 “I gan producing ooks,” Morris modstly rlatd, “with th hop o producing som which would hav a dnit claim to auty whil at th sam tim thy should  asy to rad.”30 To this nd ornamntation, spcialty typacs and “autiul and imaginativ picturs” wr mployd to crat “th most harmonious dcoration possil to th printd ook.”31 For his part, Morris dsignd Klmscott Prss typacs and ornamntal ordrs. Artists contriutd illustrations and a host o craspopl ngagd in carving woodlocks, stting typ, cutting papr, inding ooks, and othr tasks.      Two yars ar Morris’s dath, in , Klmscott Prss quipmnt

     Ovr its short litim (–), Ess Hous Prss producd

Sujcts varid, rom scns o class conict, povrty, and injustic to countrysid dpictions o pasants going aout thir afairs without an opprssor in sight.       Th coupl’s rst ook, The Queen of Fishes (), mplis thir

Th woodcuttr vows to kill th King o th Forst and rounds up a group o mn to cut and urn down th woods. Th Qun o Fishs thn plads with th rivr airis to intrvn: “Sh told thm how th autiul orst was ing dstroyd so that th land would  dry and arrn and th rivr springs drid up and upon haring this thy wr prsuadd to hlp hr.”83 Th airis rval thir displasur to th mn, who rus to carry out th uncl’s ordrs. ## P
## by GATS

Whn I was a young punk living in th middl o nowhr, I was rummaging through uildings I thought wr aandond. I ound a o o old pamphlts, on o which was aout Food Not Boms, a asic modl or starting a soup kitchn using salvagd produc.

     My rind said, “No, it’s just lik a ig hous with an industrial kitchn
whr thy hlp popl.”

ovrwhlming mysl trying to organiz way too many projcts, I dcidd to mov to th Bay Ara, whr a lot o what I was intrstd in was alrady

C., among othrs, Cliv Phillips-Wolly’s Big Game Shooting (Badminton Lirary), which contains cllnt illustrations o various spcis living togthr in East Arica.  Our Tungus huntr, who was going to marry, and thror was promptd y th dsir o gtting as many urs as h possily could, was ating th hill-sids all day long on horsack in sarch o dr. As to th rown rat, it is known that, owing to its amphiian haits, it usually stays in th lowr parts o human dwllings (low cllars, swrs, tc.), as also on th anks o canals and rivrs; it also undrtaks distant migrations in numrlss ands. Th lack rat, on th contrary, prrs staying in our dwllings thmslvs, undr th oor, as wll as in our stals and arns. It thus is much mor posd to  trminatd y man; and w cannot maintain, with any approach to crtainty, that th lack rat is ing ithr trminatd or starvd out y th rown rat and not y man.  “But it may  urgd that whn svral closly allid spcis inhait th sam trritory, w surly ought to nd at th prsnt tim many transitional orms. . . . By my thory ths allid spcis ar dscndd rom a common parnt; and during th procss o modication, ach has com adaptd to th conditions o li o its own rgion, and has supplantd and trminatd its original parnt-orm and all th transitional varitis twn its past and prsnt stats” (Origin of Species, th d., ); also ,  (all paragraph “On Etinction”).  According to Madam Mari Pavlof, who has mad a spcial study o this sujct, thy migratd rom Asia to Arica, stayd thr som tim, and rturnd nt to Asia. Chapter iii  Nineteenth Century, Fruary , .  The Descent of Man, nd o chap. ii,  and  o th nd d.  Anthropologists who ully ndors th aov viws as rgards man nvrthlss intimat, somtims,
    that th aps liv in polygamous amilis, undr th ladrship o “a strong and jalous mal.” I do not
    know how ar that assrtion is asd upon conclusiv osrvation. But th passag rom Brhm’s Life of
    Animals, which is somtims rrrd to, can hardly  takn as vry conclusiv. It occurs in his gnral

Evn as rgards th crcopithèqus, Brhm is armativ in saying that thy “narly always liv in ands, and vry sldom in amilis” (Frnch dition, ). As to othr spcis, th vry numrs o thir ands, always containing many mals, rndr th “polygamous amily” mor than doutul urthr osrvation is vidntly wantd.  Luock, Prehistoric Times, th d., .  That tnsion o th ic-cap is admittd y most o th gologists who hav spcially studid th glacial ag. MacLnnan, Studies in Ancient History, st sris, nw dition, ; nd sris, ; L. Fison and A.W. Howitt, Kamilaroi and Kurnai, Mlourn. Ths our writrs—as has n vry truly rmarkd y Giraud Tulon—starting rom difrnt acts and difrnt gnral idas, and ollowing difrnt mthods, hav com to th sam conclusion. To Bachon w ow th notion o th matrnal amily and th matrnal succssion; to Morgan—th systm o kinship, Malayan and Turanian, and a highly gid sktch o th main phass o human volution; to MacLnnan—th law o ogny; and to Fison and Howitt—th cuadro, or schm, o th conjugal socitis in Australia. All our nd in stalishing th sam act o th trial origin o th amily. Whn Bachon rst drw attntion to th matrnal amily, in his pochmaking work, and Morgan dscrid th clan-organization—oth concurring to th almost gnral tnsion o ths orms and maintaining that th marriag laws li at th vry asis o th conscutiv stps o human volution, thy wr accusd o aggration. Howvr, th most carul rsarchs proscutd sinc, y a phalan o studnts o ancint law, hav provd that all racs o mankind ar tracs o having passd through similar stags o dvlopmnt o marriag laws, such as w now s in orc among crtain savags. C. also A. Post, Die Geschlechtsgenossenscha der Urzeit, Oldnurg .  It would  impossil to ntr hr into a discussion o th origin o th marriag rstrictions. Chapter iv  Numrlss tracs o post-pliocn laks, now disappard, ar ound ovr Cntral, Wst, and North

    Tracs o Caspian Guls, ormrly takn or old ds o th Amu, intrsct th Turcoman trritory.
    Dduction must surly  mad or tmporary, priodical oscillations. But with all that, dsiccation is
    vidnt, and it progrsss at a ormrly unpctd spd. Evn in th rlativly wt parts o SouthWst Siria, th succssion o rlial survys, rcntly pulishd y Yadrintsf, shows that villags
    hav grown up on what was, ighty yars ago, th ottom o on o th laks o th Tchany group; whil
    th othr laks o th sam group, which covrd hundrds o squar mils som y yars ago, ar now
    mr ponds. In short, th dsiccation o North-Wst Asia gos on at a rat which must  masurd y

 Such communal culturs ar known to ist in  villags out o  in th Ostrogozhsk district; in  out o  in Slavyanosrsk; in  villag communitis in Alandrovsk,  in Nikolayvsk,  in Elisathgrad. In a Grman colony th communal cultur is mad or rpaying a communal dt. All join in th work, although th dt was contractd y  housholdrs out o .  Lists o such works which cam undr th notic o th zemstvo statisticians will  ound in V.V.’s Peasant Community, –.  In th govrnmnt o Moscow th primnt was usually mad on th ld which was rsrvd or th aov-mntiond communal cultur.  Svral instancs o such and similar improvmnts wr givn in th Ocial Messenger, , Nos. –. ## A  C

Peter Kropotkin (–) was th ormost thorist o th anarchist movmnt. Born a Russian princ, h rjctd his titl to com a rvolutionary, sking a socity asd on rdom, quality, and solidarity. Imprisond or his activism in Russia and Franc, his writings includ The Conquest of Bread; Fields, Factories, and Workshops; Anarchism, AnarchistCommunism, and the State; Memoirs of a Revolutionist; and Modern Science and Anarchism. Nw ditions o his classic works Mutual Aid: A Factor of Evolution; Words of a Rebel; and The Great French Revolution, 1789–1793 hav n pulishd y PM Prss to commmorat his li and work on th cntnnial o his dath.
N.O. Bonzo is an anarchist illustrator, printmakr, and paintr asd in Portland, OR. Thy ar th crator o O with Their Heads: An Antifascist Coloring Book.

H has writtn or Harper’s, The Nation, Mute, and th New Le Review. including Living at the Edges of Capitalism: Adventures in Exile and Mutual Aid (coauthord with Dnis O’Harn); Don’t Mourn, Balkanize!; and Wobblies and Zapatistas (with Staughton Lynd). H is th ditor o th PM Prss Kairos imprint.

ABOUT PM PRESS PM Press is an independent, radical publisher of books and media to educate, entertain, and inspire. Founded in 2007 by a small group of people with decades of publishing, media, and organizing experience, PM Press amplies the voices of radical authors, artists, and activists. Our aim is to deliver bold political ideas and vital stories to all walks of life and arm the dreamers to demand the impossible. We have sold millions of copies of our books, most often one at a time, face to face. We’re old enough to know what we’re doing and young enough to know what’s at stake. Join us to create a better world.

In the years since its founding—and on a mere shoestring—PM Press has risen to the formidable challenge of publishing and distributing knowledge and entertainment for the struggles ahead. With over 450 releases to date, we have published an impressive and stimulating array of literature, art, music, politics, and culture. Using every available medium, we’ve succeeded in connecting those hungry for ideas and information to those putting them into practice.

DEPARTMENT OF ANTHROPOLOGY & SOCIAL CHANGE Anthropology and Social Change, housed within the California Institute of Integral Studies, is a small innovative graduate department with a particular focus on activist scholarship, militant research, and social change. We oer both masters and doctoral degree programs.
Our unique approach to collaborative research methodology dissolves traditional barriers between research and political activism, between insiders and outsiders, and between researchers and protagonists. Activist research is a tool for “creating the conditions we describe.” We engage in the process of co-research to explore existing alternatives and possibilities for social change.
Anthropology and Social Change anth@ciis.edu 1453 Mission Street 94103 San Francisco, California www.ciis.edu/academics/graduate-programs/anthropology-and-socialchange
Words of a Rebel Peter Kropotkin Translated and edited by Iain McKay with a Preface by Elisée Reclus ISBN: –––– . pages
Peter Kropotkin remains one of the best-known anarchist thinkers, and Words of a Rebel was his rst libertarian book. Published in 1885 while he was in a French jail for anarchist activism, this collection of articles from the newspaper Le Revolté sees Kropotkin criticise the failings of capitalism and those who seek to end it by means of its main support, the state. Instead, he urged the creation of a mass movement from below that would expropriate property and destroy the state, replacing their centralised hierarchies with federations of self-governing communities and workplaces.
Kropotkin’s instant classic included discussions themes and ideas he returned to repeatedly during his ve decades in the anarchist movement. Unsurprisingly, Words of a Rebel was soon translated into numerous languages—including Italian, Spanish, Bulgarian, Russian, and Chinese—and reprinted time and time again. But despite its inuence as Kropotkin’s rst anarchist work, it was the last to be completely translated into English.
This is a new translation from the French original by Iain McKay except for a few chapters previously translated by Nicolas Walter. Both anarchist activists and writers, they are well placed to understand the assumptions within and inuences on Kropotkin’s revolutionary journalism. It includes all the original 1885 text along with the preface to the 1904 Italian as well as the preface and afterward to the 1919 Russian editions. In addition, it includes many articles on the labour movement written by Kropotkin for Le Revolté which show how he envisioned getting from criticism to a social revolution. Along with a comprehensive glossary and an introduction by Iain McKay placing this work within the history of anarchism as well as indicating its relevance to radicals and revolutionaries today, this is the denitive edition of an anarchist classic.
“Peter Kropotkin was a giant of socialist history whose tireless scientic, historical, and political scholarship and agitational writing united and fueled the transnational anarchist movement of the turn of the twentieth century. But this aristocrat turned revolutionary didn’t start there. Words of a Rebel sheds light on the young Kropotkin’s political transformation in the wake of the destruction of the First International. By including articles from Le Revolté, this volume traces Kropotkin’s political journey farther as he sewed the early seeds of anarchist communism and set an agenda for anti-authoritarian rebellion for years to come.” —Mark Bray, author of Antifa: The Anti-Fascist Handbook and coeditor of
## Anarchist Education and the Modern School

The Great French Revolution, 1789–1793 Peter Kropotkin with an Introduction by David Berry ISBN: –––– . pages
The Great French Revolution, 1789–1793 is Peter Kropotkin’s most substantial historical work. In it he presents a people’s history of the world-shaking events of the Revolution and shows the key role the working men and women of the towns and countryside played in it. Without the constant pressure of popular organisations and activity, the politicians would never have created a Republic, nor been able to survive the counterrevolutionary forces internally or externally.
Focusing on such mass movements—and especially the peasant majority— rather than on the few great men beloved of bourgeois accounts, this is a groundbreaking account of the period and a seminal work of “history from below.” Later research may have corrected some factual details and opened new avenues of scholarship, but Kropotkin’s text remains an exemplar of anarchist history-writing, challenging both bourgeois republican and Marxist interpretations of the Revolution.
Yet it is more than a history: Kropotkin uses the experience of the French Revolution to aid us in our current struggles and to learn its lessons in order to ensure the success of future revolutions. This book raises issues which have resurfaced time and again, as well as oering solutions based on the self-activity of the masses, the new, decentralised, directly democratic social organisations they forged during the Revolution, and the need to transform a political revolt into a social revolution which seeks to secure the well-being of all by transforming the economy from the start.
“The French Revolution erupted out of the remnants of the old world and set a dynamic precedent for new centuries of resistance. Multifaceted, contradictory, and compelling, the French Revolution cast an enormous shadow that inuenced every radical faction of 19th century politics. Peter Kropotkin was perhaps the preeminent anarchist intellect of his generation, and so his book The Great French Revolution, 1789–1793 provides us with a fascinating exploration into the late 19th century anarchist vision of historical transformation. This saga of popular upheaval from below provides a fascinating mirror image of how Kropotkin and many of his comrades envisioned the coming revolution.” —Mark Bray, author of Antifa: The Anti-Fascist Handbook and co-editor of Anarchist Education and the Modern School: A Francisco Ferrer Reader
“In this classic text, Kropotkin demonstrates how even struggles that falter can lay the groundwork for subsequent upheavals. The French Revolution may have succumbed to reaction, but it also gave birth to ideas that would dene revolutions to come. A must-read for anyone struggling to put insurgency on the agenda once again.” —AK Thompson, author of Black Bloc, White Riot
Anarchism, Anarchist Communism, and The State: Three Essays Peter Kropotkin with an Introduction by Brian Morris and bibliographic notes by Iain McKay ISBN: –––– . pages
Amid the clashes, complexities, and political personalities of world politics in the late nineteenth and early twentieth centuries, Peter Kropotkin stands out. Born a prince in Tsarist Russia, sent to Siberia to learn his militaristic, aristocratic trade, he instead renounced his titles and took up the “beautiful idea” of anarchism. Across a continent he would become known as a passionate advocate of a world without borders, without kings and bosses.
From a Russian cell to France, to London and Brighton, he used his extraordinary mind to dissect the birth of State power and then present a dierent vision, one in which the human impulse to liberty can be found throughout history, undying even in times of defeat. In the three essays presented here, Kropotkin attempted to distill his many insights into brief but brilliant essays on the state, anarchism, and the ideology for which he became a founding name—anarchist communism.
With a detailed and rich introduction from Brian Morris, and accompanied by bibliographic notes from Iain McKay, this collection contextualises and contemporises three of Kropotkin’s most inuential essays.
“In this collection of essays, Kropotkin excels in his grasp of the state, its dynamics, and the social relations out of which it emerges, dovetailed with his radical vision for libertarian egalitarian social change. Including an informative foreword by Brian Morris on the great anarchist’s colourful life, and Kropotkin’s own extended analysis of the origins of anarchism, the book goes to the core of what makes Kropotkin’s work so stimulating: he is peculiarly capable, through detailed historical accounts and discussions of his own times, of somehow speaking to our own contemporary dilemmas and challenges.” —Anthony Ince, coeditor of Historical Geographies of Anarchism
“This is one of the most excellent introductions to anarchism, putting paid to the usual objections to the system, synonymous as it has become, wrongly, with disorganisation and chaos.”
## —Workers Solidarity

Kropotkin: The Politics of Community Brian Morris ISBN: –––– . pages
The nineteenth century witnessed the growth of anarchist literature, which advocated a society based on voluntary cooperation without government authority. Although his classical writings on mutual aid and the philosophy of anarchism are still published today, Peter Kropotkin remains a neglected gure. A talented geographer and a revolutionary socialist, Kropotkin was one of the most important theoreticians of the anarchist movement.
In Kropotkin: The Politics of Community, Brian Morris rearms with an attitude of critical sympathy the contemporary relevance of Kropotkin as a political and moral philosopher and as a pioneering social ecologist. Wellresearched and wide-ranging, this volume not only presents an important contribution to the history of anarchism, both as a political tradition and as a social movement, but also oers insightful reections on contemporary debates in political theory and ecological thought. After a short biographical note, the book analyzes in four parts Kropotkin’s writings on anarchist communism, agrarian socialism, and integral education; modern science and evolutionary theory; the French Revolution and the modern state; and possessive individualism, terror, and war.
Standing as a comprehensive and engaging introduction to anarchism, social ecology, and the philosophy of evolutionary holism, Kropotkin is written in a straightforward manner that will appeal to those interested in social anarchism and in alternatives to neoliberal doctrines.
“Peter Kropotkin has been largely ignored as a utopian crackpot, but Brian Morris demonstrates in this wide-ranging and detailed analysis that Kropotkin addressed signicantly and perceptively the major issues of the present day.” —Harold B. Barclay, author of People without Government: An Anthropology of
## Anarchy
